5d05f20 iter 3: ammo + R-reload + crosshair + HUD ammo indicator +37 -3
.hip-log/RUNS.md, index.html, src/main.js, src/systems/shooting.js
Post-mortem:

First attempt stopped after just reading the layout (2 rounds, 135 ctok). The v0.3.27 system prompt's "no narration, terse final response" rules appear to overcorrect for some prompts — the model decided it was done. Retry with imperative phrasing ("USE THE WRITE TOOL", "DO NOT just describe — write it") + spelled-out 4-step recipe (write → node -c → git add → git commit) succeeded in 35s. **Loop lesson:** When a task is a "creation" (writing a new file), the prompt needs to be imperative about USE THE WRITE TOOL and list the exact bash steps. Future iters that involve creating new files should follow this pattern.

Post-mortem:

22 rounds and 15.6K ctok over 11:40 wall, but only 2 lines of diff committed (import + `const phone = createPhone()`). The model likely got stuck trying to apply a multi-line `if (!phone.isOpen()) { ... }` gate around several existing update calls — that pattern is genuinely awkward via a single `edit` (large old_string needed to disambiguate the location, and the gate has to wrap exactly the right calls without breaking the existing scope). The model probably attempted the gate edit multiple times, hit drift / ambiguity errors, kept retrying, and exited rounds=22 with the gate not landed. The import and instantiation it DID land cleanly. **Loop lesson:** dispatches that require wrapping existing multi-line code in a conditional are higher risk than dispatches that just insert standalone lines or replace specific identifiers. Mitigation: instead of asking the model to wrap-existing-code-in-conditional, ask it to factor the existing update calls into a small helper function and then call that helper conditionally. The helper is a clean insertion + one short edit at the call site, both surgical.

f01fa3b loop iter 39: clouds feature complete via partial+follow-up; staleness pattern noted +10 -3
LOOP_REPORT.md, TODO.md
Post-mortem:

Staleness mid-edit (`src/main.js changed since last read at X (now mtime Y); read it again before editing`) blocked hip's 3rd edit. Hip stopped after the staleness error rather than re-reading. Orchestrator committed the 2-edit partial then dispatched a tight follow-up that landed clean in 22s. Net cost: 1 extra dispatch + ~25s. Not bad given the recovery was automatic. **Loop lesson tentative:** when a hip dispatch needs ≥3 sequential edits to the SAME file, the staleness check sometimes fires between edits because hip's bash tool calls (the in-edit `git add`?) touch the file mtime. Mitigation idea for future: prefer multi_edit (single tool call) over multiple back-to-back edit calls on the same file. Have NOT seen this yet on multi_edit because hip's tool registry intentionally lacks it (per memory: qwen3 XML can't reliably serialize multi_edit's array-of-objects). Bear with the staleness-then-follow-up pattern for now — it self-heals.

Files in commits: LOOP_REPORT.md, TODO.md
7e0e330 loop iter 49: FAILED (23b multi-file wire burned 15min/28K ctok, no commit); deferred +11 -1
LOOP_REPORT.md, TODO.md
Post-mortem:

Hip ran 30 rounds, generated 28,693 completion tokens across 15:40 wall, and ended with `success=True` per its own log — but working tree was CLEAN after. Zero file changes, zero commits. This is the same failure shape as iter 2 (also a multi-file edit prompt that asked hip to discover-then-edit two existing files). Pattern: when the spec says "edit file A AND file B, where the touch points need to be discovered" and there's no obvious anchor pattern, hip drifts through searches and reads forever, hits intermittent edit-staleness or matching errors, then exits without committing. **Lesson:** multi-file edit prompts that span >1 large existing file (shooting.js ~120 lines + vehicle.js ~250 lines) without specific line/symbol anchors are over the model's reliability threshold under the current Loop pattern. Mitigation: for such tasks, split into 2 iters even at the wiring layer. E.g. iter 49a = "in shooting.js find the bullet-hit dispatch, return only the line number range" (effectively a read-only locate iter), then iter 49b = "at line N in shooting.js, insert this exact snippet." That's an option for the next 23b retry. For now: 23b deferred. Cron continues with the next TODO.

[ok]      1	# AGENTS.md — Project Module Map
     2	
     3	## src/main.js
     4	Top-level entry point; wires all entities, systems, and scene modules; sets up game loop, renderer, and input handling.
     5	
     6	## src/entities/
     7	- `player.js` — Player character: movement, health, state, input handling.
     8	- `enemy.js` — Enemy AI: spawning, chasing, attacking, death.
     9	- `npcs.js` — Civilian NPCs: wandering, fleeing, idle behavior.
    10	- `vehicle.js` — Drivable vehicles: physics, collision, player entry/exit.
    11	- `police.js` — Police units: pursuit, wanted-level response.
    12	- `pickups.js` — Collectible items: health packs, ammo, score pickups.
    13	- `barrels.js` — Destructible barrels: explosion triggers, placement.
    14	- `target.js` — Target dummies: shooting practice, hit detection.
    15	
    16	## src/systems/
    17	- `shooting.js` — Raycast/projectile shooting mechanics.
    18	- `weapons.js` — Weapon definitions, switching, stats, ammo.
    19	- `audio.js` — SFX playback (shots, explosions, pickups).
    20	- `music.js` — Background music, dynamic intensity layers.
    21	- `missions.js` — Mission objectives, completion tracking.
    22	- `minimap.js` — Radar/minimap rendering and entity markers.
    23	- `wanted.js` — Wanted level system, police escalation.
    24	- `grenades.js` — Grenade throwing, arming, explosion logic.
    25	- `particles.js` — Particle effects (explosions, smoke, sparks).
    26	- `weather.js` — Weather effects (rain, fog, visibility).
    27	- `save.js` — Save/load game state to localStorage.
    28	- `pause.js` — Pause menu, game state freeze.
    29	- `hit-marker.js` — Hit feedback visual markers.
    30	- `stamina.js` — Stamina bar for sprinting/exertion.
    31	- `streak.js` — Kill streak tracking and rewards.
    32	- `muzzle-flash.js` — Muzzle flash visual effects.
    33	- `feedback.js` — Screen shake, damage flash, general feedback.
    34	
    35	## src/scene/
    36	- `city.js` — City buildings, streets, urban geometry.
    37	- `world.js` — World container, terrain, skybox setup.
    38	- `props.js` — Static props (crates, signs, furniture).
    39	- `mountains.js` — Distant mountain geometry, backdrop.
    40	
    41	## How to add a new feature
    42	- **Top-level wiring:** import and register in `src/main.js` (game loop, init order).
    43	- **Entities** (things with position/state) go in `src/entities/`.
    44	- **Systems** (behaviors, effects, UI) go in `src/systems/`.

    83	    return false;
    84	  }

    86	  function isPlayerNear() { return lastNear; }

Post-mortem:

Reused the iter 54 session for the wire-up. ctok dropped from 102 → 90 even though the wire involved 3 edits to a 700-line main.js, because animals.js itself was in cache. This confirms the cache-warming policy of "standalone + wire as consecutive resumed-session iters" — fastest path for split tasks. The same model would have spent ~1500-2500 ctok exploring main.js on a fresh session before the first edit.

[0;33mpath[0m:  /Users/dan/.hip-loop/3d-shooter/AGENTS.md
[ok]      1	# AGENTS.md — Project Module Map
     2	
     3	## src/main.js
     4	Top-level entry point; wires all entities, systems, and scene modules; sets up game loop, renderer, and input handling.
     5	
     6	## src/entities/
     7	- `player.js` — Player character: movement, health, state, input handling.
     8	- `enemy.js` — Enemy AI: spawning, chasing, attacking, death.
     9	- `npcs.js` — Civilian NPCs: wandering, fleeing, idle behavior.
    10	- `vehicle.js` — Drivable vehicles: physics, collision, player entry/exit.
    11	- `police.js` — Police units: pursuit, wanted-level response.
    12	- `pickups.js` — Collectible items: health packs, ammo, score pickups.
    13	- `barrels.js` — Destructible barrels: explosion triggers, placement.
    14	- `target.js` — Target dummies: shooting practice, hit detection.
    15	
    16	## src/systems/
    17	- `shooting.js` — Raycast/projectile shooting mechanics.
    18	- `weapons.js` — Weapon definitions, switching, stats, ammo.
    19	- `audio.js` — SFX playback (shots, explosions, pickups).
    20	- `music.js` — Background music, dynamic intensity layers.
    21	- `missions.js` — Mission objectives, completion tracking.
    22	- `minimap.js` — Radar/minimap rendering and entity markers.
    23	- `wanted.js` — Wanted level system, police escalation.
    24	- `grenades.js` — Grenade throwing, arming, explosion logic.
    25	- `particles.js` — Particle effects (explosions, smoke, sparks).
    26	- `weather.js` — Weather effects (rain, fog, visibility).
    27	- `save.js` — Save/load game state to localStorage.
    28	- `pause.js` — Pause menu, game state freeze.
    29	- `hit-marker.js` — Hit feedback visual markers.
    30	- `stamina.js` — Stamina bar for sprinting/exertion.
    31	- `streak.js` — Kill streak tracking and rewards.
    32	- `muzzle-flash.js` — Muzzle flash visual effects.
    33	- `feedback.js` — Screen shake, damage flash, general feedback.
    34	
    35	## src/scene/
    36	- `city.js` — City buildings, streets, urban geometry.
    37	- `world.js` — World container, terrain, skybox setup.
    38	- `props.js` — Static props (crates, signs, furniture).
    39	- `mountains.js` — Distant mountain geometry, backdrop.
    40	
    41	## How to add a new feature
    42	- **Top-level wiring:** import and register in `src/main.js` (game loop, init order).
    43	- **Entities** (things with position/state) go in `src/entities/`.
    44	- **Systems** (behaviors, effects, UI) go in `src/systems/`.

[0;33mpath[0m:  /Users/dan/.hip-loop/3d-shooter/src/scene/clouds.js
[ok]      1	export function createClouds(THREE, opts = {}) {
     2	  const count = opts.count ?? 14;
     3	  const range = opts.range ?? 200;
     4	  const minY = opts.minY ?? 35;
     5	  const maxY = opts.maxY ?? 45;
     6	  const driftSpeed = opts.driftSpeed ?? 2.5;
     7	  const group = new THREE.Group();
     8	  const clouds = [];
     9	
    10	  for (let i = 0; i < count; i++) {
    11	    const cloud = new THREE.Group();
    12	    const puffs = Math.floor(3 + Math.random() * 3);
    13	    for (let p = 0; p < puffs; p++) {
    14	      const w = 4 + Math.random() * 5;
    15	      const h = 1 + Math.random();
    16	      const d = 4 + Math.random() * 5;
    17	      const puff = new THREE.Mesh(
    18	        new THREE.BoxGeometry(w, h, d),
    19	        new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ color: 0xffffff, roughness: 0.95 }),
    20	      );
    21	      puff.position.set(
    22	        (Math.random() - 0.5) * 6,
    23	        (Math.random() - 0.5) * 1,
    24	        (Math.random() - 0.5) * 6,
    25	      );
    26	      cloud.add(puff);
    27	    }
    28	    cloud.position.set(
    29	      (Math.random() - 0.5) * range * 2,
    30	      minY + Math.random() * (maxY - minY),
    31	      (Math.random() - 0.5) * range * 2,
    32	    );
    33	    group.add(cloud);
    34	    clouds.push(cloud);
    35	  }
    36	
    37	  function update(dt) {
    38	    const drift = dt * driftSpeed;
    39	    for (const c of clouds) {
    40	      c.position.x += drift;
    41	      if (c.position.x > range) c.position.x -= range * 2;
    42	    }
    43	  }
    44	
    45	  return { group, update };
    46	}

a2ce8a7 iter 57: wire construction zone into main.js (27b) +4 -0
src/main.js
Post-mortem:

First wire used `construction.position.set(...)` and `scene.add(construction)` — but the factory returns `{ group }`, so `construction.position` was undefined. Build passed (it's valid JS), runtime crashed (browser caught it). Fix dispatched in same session, 1 edit / 34 ctok / ~5s. **Loop lesson:** when wiring a standalone module, always include the module's return shape in the wire prompt verbatim (`returns { group, update }` etc.). My iter 57 prompt erroneously said "returns a bare THREE.Group" — model trusted the prompt over re-reading the source. Putting the actual return signature in the wire-up prompt would have prevented it. Updated LOOP_RULES context-inputs to require this.

[0;33mpath[0m:  /Users/dan/.hip-loop/3d-shooter/AGENTS.md
[ok]      1	# AGENTS.md — Project Module Map
     2	
     3	## src/main.js
     4	Top-level entry point; wires all entities, systems, and scene modules; sets up game loop, renderer, and input handling.
     5	
     6	## src/entities/
     7	- `player.js` — Player character: movement, health, state, input handling.
     8	- `enemy.js` — Enemy AI: spawning, chasing, attacking, death.
     9	- `npcs.js` — Civilian NPCs: wandering, fleeing, idle behavior.
    10	- `vehicle.js` — Drivable vehicles: physics, collision, player entry/exit.
    11	- `police.js` — Police units: pursuit, wanted-level response.
    12	- `pickups.js` — Collectible items: health packs, ammo, score pickups.
    13	- `barrels.js` — Destructible barrels: explosion triggers, placement.
    14	- `target.js` — Target dummies: shooting practice, hit detection.
    15	
    16	## src/systems/
    17	- `shooting.js` — Raycast/projectile shooting mechanics.
    18	- `weapons.js` — Weapon definitions, switching, stats, ammo.
    19	- `audio.js` — SFX playback (shots, explosions, pickups).
    20	- `music.js` — Background music, dynamic intensity layers.
    21	- `missions.js` — Mission objectives, completion tracking.
    22	- `minimap.js` — Radar/minimap rendering and entity markers.
    23	- `wanted.js` — Wanted level system, police escalation.
    24	- `grenades.js` — Grenade throwing, arming, explosion logic.
    25	- `particles.js` — Particle effects (explosions, smoke, sparks).
    26	- `weather.js` — Weather effects (rain, fog, visibility).
    27	- `save.js` — Save/load game state to localStorage.
    28	- `pause.js` — Pause menu, game state freeze.
    29	- `hit-marker.js` — Hit feedback visual markers.
    30	- `stamina.js` — Stamina bar for sprinting/exertion.
    31	- `streak.js` — Kill streak tracking and rewards.
    32	- `muzzle-flash.js` — Muzzle flash visual effects.
    33	- `feedback.js` — Screen shake, damage flash, general feedback.
    34	
    35	## src/scene/
    36	- `city.js` — City buildings, streets, urban geometry.
    37	- `world.js` — World container, terrain, skybox setup.
    38	- `props.js` — Static props (crates, signs, furniture).
    39	- `mountains.js` — Distant mountain geometry, backdrop.
    40	
    41	## How to add a new feature
    42	- **Top-level wiring:** import and register in `src/main.js` (game loop, init order).
    43	- **Entities** (things with position/state) go in `src/entities/`.
    44	- **Systems** (behaviors, effects, UI) go in `src/systems/`.

     2	  const group = new THREE.Group();
     3

     5	  const groundGeo = new THREE.BoxGeometry(30, 0.05, 30);
     6	  const groundMat = new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ color: 0xc2a670 });
     7	  const ground = new THREE.Mesh(groundGeo, groundMat);
     8	  ground.position.set(0, 0.025, 0);
     9	  group.add(ground);
    10	
    11	  // Crane mast
    12	  const mastGeo = new THREE.CylinderGeometry(0.4, 0.4, 12);
    13	  const craneMat = new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ color: 0xff6600 });
    14	  const mast = new THREE.Mesh(mastGeo, craneMat);
    15	  mast.position.set(-8, 6, -8);
    16	  group.add(mast);
    17

    22	  group.add(arm);

    27	  const cable = new THREE.Mesh(cableGeo, cableMat);
    28	  cable.position.set(-8, 9.3, 2);

    34	  hook.position.set(-8, 6.6, 2);
    35	  group.add(hook);

    38	  const coneGeo = new THREE.CylinderGeometry(0.2, 0.4, 0.7, 8);
    39	  const coneMat = new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ color: 0xff6600 });
    40	  const conePositions = [
    41	    [-10, 0.35, -10],
    42	    [-5, 0.35, -10],
    43	    [0, 0.35, -10],
    44	    [5, 0.35, -10],

    48	  for (const [x, y, z] of conePositions) {
    49	    const cone = new THREE.Mesh(coneGeo, coneMat);
    50	    cone.position.set(x, y, z);
    51	    group.add(cone);
    52	  }
    53	
    54	  // Striped barriers (3 in a row along x)
    55	  const stripeOrange = new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ color: 0xff6600 });
    56	  const stripeWhite = new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ color: 0xffffff });
    57	  const stripeGeo = new THREE.BoxGeometry(2, 0.4, 0.2);
    58	  const barrierPositions = [
    59	    [8, 0.2, 8],
    60	    [5, 0.2, 8],
    61	    [2, 0.2, 8],
    62	  ];
    63	  for (const [bx, by, bz] of barrierPositions) {
    64	    const barrier = new THREE.Group();
    65	    const mats = [stripeOrange, stripeWhite, stripeOrange, stripeWhite];
    66	    for (let i = 0; i < 4; i++) {
    67	      const stripe = new THREE.Mesh(stripeGeo, mats[i]);
    68	      stripe.position.y = (i - 1.5) * 0.4;
    69	      barrier.add(stripe);
    70	    }
    71	    barrier.position.set(bx, by, bz);
    72	    group.add(barrier);
    73	  }
    74	
    75	  // Dirt pile
    76	  const dirtGeo = new THREE.ConeGeometry(2, 1.5, 8);

    78	  const dirt = new THREE.Mesh(dirtGeo, dirtMat);
    79	  dirt.position.set(10, 0.75, 5);
    80	  group.add(dirt);

    82	  // Chain-link fence posts (4 corners)
    83	  const postGeo = new THREE.BoxGeometry(0.05, 1.5, 30);
    84	  const postMat = new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ color: 0x888888 });
    85	  const postPositions = [

Hip dispatch log (last 8k chars) 
[0;33mnew_string[0m:  import { MathUtils } from 'three';
            
            export function createStunts() {
              let inStunt = false;
              let stuntTimer = 0;
              let currentRamp = null;
            
              const overlay = document.createElement('div');
              overlay.style.cssText = [
                'position:fixed',
                'top:20px',
                'left:0',
                'right:0',
                'text-align:center',
                'font-weight:bold',
                'color:#ffd400',
                'font-size:48px',
                'pointer-events:none',
                'display:none',
                'font-family:sans-serif',
                'text-shadow:0 0 10px rgba(0,0,0,0.8)',
                'z-index:9999',
              ].join(';');
              overlay.textContent = 'STUNT BONUS!';
              document.body.appendChild(overlay);
            
              function showOverlay() { overlay.style.display = 'block'; }
              function hideOverlay() { overlay.style.display = 'none'; }
            
              function endStunt() {
                inStunt = false;
                currentRamp = null;
                stuntTimer = 0;
                hideOverlay();
              }
            
              function update(dt, playerPos, playerVel, isAirborne, ramps) {
                if (inStunt) {
                  stuntTimer += dt;
                  if (stuntTimer >= 2.5 || (!isAirborne && stuntTimer >= 0.3)) {
                    endStunt();
                  }
                  return;
                }
            
                if (!isAirborne) return;
            
                for (const ramp of ramps) {
                  const dx = playerPos.x - ramp.position.x;
                  const dz = playerPos.z - ramp.position.z;
                  const dist = Math.sqrt(dx * dx + dz * dz);
                  const footprint = Math.max(ramp.length, 5);
                  if (dist > footprint) continue;
            
                  const hVelX = playerVel.x;
                  const hVelZ = playerVel.z;
                  const dirX = ramp.direction.x;
                  const dirZ = ramp.direction.z;
                  const dot = hVelX * dirX + hVelZ * dirZ;
            
                  if (dot > 1) {
                    inStunt = true;
                    stuntTimer = 0;
                    currentRamp = ramp;
                    showOverlay();
                    break;
                  }
                }
              }
            
              function isInStunt() { return inStunt; }
            
              function getTimeScale() { return inStunt ? 0.4 : 1.0; }
            
              return { update, isInStunt, getTimeScale };
            }

[0;33mpath[0m:  /Users/dan/.hip-loop/3d-shooter/src/scene/clouds.js
[ok]      1	export function createClouds(THREE, opts = {}) {
     2	  const count = opts.count ?? 14;
     3	  const range = opts.range ?? 200;
     4	  const minY = opts.minY ?? 35;
     5	  const maxY = opts.maxY ?? 45;
     6	  const driftSpeed = opts.driftSpeed ?? 2.5;
     7	  const group = new THREE.Group();
     8	  const clouds = [];
     9	
    10	  for (let i = 0; i < count; i++) {
    11	    const cloud = new THREE.Group();
    12	    const puffs = Math.floor(3 + Math.random() * 3);
    13	    for (let p = 0; p < puffs; p++) {
    14	      const w = 4 + Math.random() * 5;
    15	      const h = 1 + Math.random();
    16	      const d = 4 + Math.random() * 5;
    17	      const puff = new THREE.Mesh(
    18	        new THREE.BoxGeometry(w, h, d),
    19	        new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ color: 0xffffff, roughness: 0.95 }),
    20	      );
    21	      puff.position.set(
    22	        (Math.random() - 0.5) * 6,
    23	        (Math.random() - 0.5) * 1,
    24	        (Math.random() - 0.5) * 6,
    25	      );
    26	      cloud.add(puff);
    27	    }
    28	    cloud.position.set(
    29	      (Math.random() - 0.5) * range * 2,
    30	      minY + Math.random() * (maxY - minY),
    31	      (Math.random() - 0.5) * range * 2,
    32	    );
    33	    group.add(cloud);
    34	    clouds.push(cloud);
    35	  }
    36	
    37	  function update(dt) {
    38	    const drift = dt * driftSpeed;
    39	    for (const c of clouds) {
    40	      c.position.x += drift;
    41	      if (c.position.x > range) c.position.x -= range * 2;
    42	    }
    43	  }
    44	
    45	  return { group, update };
    46	}

[0;33mpath[0m:  /Users/dan/.hip-loop/3d-shooter/src/systems/stamina.js
[ok]      1	// Stamina system: [0,100], regen when idle, drain when sprinting.
     2	export function createStamina() {
     3	  let value = 100;
     4	  let isDraining = false;
     5	  let graceTimer = 0; // 1s grace before regen starts
     6	
     7	  const REGEN_RATE = 18; // per sec
     8	  const DRAIN_RATE = 30; // per sec
     9	  const GRACE_DURATION = 1.0; // sec
    10	  const SPRINT_THRESHOLD = 5;
    11	  const RECOVER_THRESHOLD = 25;
    12	
    13	  return {
    14	    get() { return value; },
    15	
    16	    drain(dt) {
    17	      isDraining = true;
    18	      graceTimer = 0;
    19	      value = Math.max(0, value - DRAIN_RATE * dt);
    20	    },
    21	
    22	    regen(dt) {
    23	      isDraining = false;
    24	      if (graceTimer < GRACE_DURATION) {
    25	        graceTimer += dt;
    26	        return;
    27	      }
    28	      value = Math.min(100, value + REGEN_RATE * dt);
    29	    },
    30	
    31	    canSprint() { return value > SPRINT_THRESHOLD; },
    32	
    33	    isExhausted() { return value <= 0; },
    34	
    35	    canRecoverFromExhausted() { return value > RECOVER_THRESHOLD; },
    36	
    37	    isDraining() { return isDraining; },
    38	  };
    39	}

     8	function rand(min, max) { return min + Math.random() * (max - min); }
     9	
    10	// Simple heightmap-based mountain: cone-like shape with noise
    11	function createMountainMesh(height, baseRadius, color) {
    12	  const geo = new THREE.ConeGeometry(baseRadius, height, 7, 4);
    13	  // Distort vertices for organic look
    14	  const pos = geo.attributes.position;
    15	  for (let i = 0; i < pos.count; i++) {
    16	    const x = pos.getX(i);
    17	    const y = pos.getY(i);
    18	    const z = pos.getZ(i);
    19	    // Skip the apex (top vertex)
    20	    if (y === height / 2) continue;
    21	    const noise = rand(-baseRadius * 0.3, baseRadius * 0.3);
    22	    pos.setX(i, x + noise * 0.5);
    23	    pos.setZ(i, z + noise * 0.5);
    24	  }
    25	  geo.computeVertexNormals();
    26	  const mat = new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({
    27	    color,
    28	    roughness: 0.9,
    29	    flatShading: true,
    30	  });
    31	  return new THREE.Mesh(geo, mat);
    32	}
    33	
    34	export function createMountains(scene) {
    35	  const mountainGroup = new THREE.Group();
    36	  mountainGroup.name = 'mountains';
    37	
    38	  // Mountain palette: earthy greys/browns
    39	  const colors = [0x5a6b5a, 0x6b5e5a, 0x556666, 0x665555, 0x5e6b5e, 0x5a5a6b];
    40	
    41	  // Place mountains in a ring around the city
    42	  const count = 30;
    43	  for (let i = 0; i < count; i++) {
    44	    const angle = (i / count) * Math.PI * 2 + rand(-0.15, 0.15);
    45	    const dist = CITY_RADIUS + rand(10, 40); // 98-128 units from center
    46	
    47	    const x = Math.cos(angle) * dist;
    48	    const z = Math.sin(angle) * dist;
    49	
    50	    const height = rand(25, 55);
    51	    const baseRadius = rand(12, 25);
    52	    const color = colors[Math.floor(rand(0, colors.length))];
    53	
    54	    const mesh = createMountainMesh(height, baseRadius, color);
    55	    mesh.position.set(x, height / 2 - 5, z);
    56	    mesh.rotation.y = rand(0, Math.PI * 2);
    57	    mesh.castShadow = true;
    58	    mesh.receiveShadow = true;
    59	    mountainGroup.add(mesh);
    60	  }
    61	
    62	  // Add a few larger "peak" mountains for variety
    63	  for (let i = 0; i < 6; i++) {
    64	    const angle = (i / 6) * Math.PI * 2 + rand(-0.2, 0.2);
    65	    const dist = CITY_RADIUS + rand(25, 50);
    66	
    67	    const x = Math.cos(angle) * dist;
    68	    const z = Math.sin(angle) * dist;
    69	
    70	    const height = rand(50, 80);

src/entities/vehicles/motorcycle.js
Post-mortem:

Same shape as iter 70: motorcycle already had handlebars/headlight/exhaust from iter 14. Hip swapped existing geometries to match the new spec (Cylinder → Box handlebars, plain mat → emissive headlight, plain → chrome+metalness exhaust). Net: 9 deletions / 9 insertions, zero new lines. Skipped the seat (not strictly needed; bike has the visual differentiation already). This is becoming a useful trend: the model "completes" specs by retuning rather than duplicating — keeps file size in check.

     2	
     3	## src/main.js
     4	Top-level entry point; wires all entities, systems, and scene modules; sets up game loop, renderer, and input handling.

     6	## src/entities/
     7	- `player.js` — Player character: movement, health, state, input handling.
     8	- `enemy.js` — Enemy AI: spawning, chasing, attacking, death.
     9	- `npcs.js` — Civilian NPCs: wandering, fleeing, idle behavior.
    10	- `vehicle.js` — Drivable vehicles: physics, collision, player entry/exit.
    11	- `police.js` — Police units: pursuit, wanted-level response.
    12	- `pickups.js` — Collectible items: health packs, ammo, score pickups.
    13	- `barrels.js` — Destructible barrels: explosion triggers, placement.
    14	- `target.js` — Target dummies: shooting practice, hit detection.
    15	
    16	## src/systems/
    17	- `shooting.js` — Raycast/projectile shooting mechanics.
    18	- `weapons.js` — Weapon definitions, switching, stats, ammo.
    19	- `audio.js` — SFX playback (shots, explosions, pickups).
    20	- `music.js` — Background music, dynamic intensity layers.
    21	- `missions.js` — Mission objectives, completion tracking.
    22	- `minimap.js` — Radar/minimap rendering and entity markers.
    23	- `wanted.js` — Wanted level system, police escalation.
    24	- `grenades.js` — Grenade throwing, arming, explosion logic.
    25	- `particles.js` — Particle effects (explosions, smoke, sparks).
    26	- `weather.js` — Weather effects (rain, fog, visibility).
    27	- `save.js` — Save/load game state to localStorage.
    28	- `pause.js` — Pause menu, game state freeze.
    29	- `hit-marker.js` — Hit feedback visual markers.
    30	- `stamina.js` — Stamina bar for sprinting/exertion.
    31	- `streak.js` — Kill streak tracking and rewards.
    32	- `muzzle-flash.js` — Muzzle flash visual effects.
    33	- `feedback.js` — Screen shake, damage flash, general feedback.
    34	
    35	## src/scene/
    36	- `city.js` — City buildings, streets, urban geometry.
    37	- `world.js` — World container, terrain, skybox setup.
    38	- `props.js` — Static props (crates, signs, furniture).
    39	- `mountains.js` — Distant mountain geometry, backdrop.
    40	
    41	## How to add a new feature
    42	- **Top-level wiring:** import and register in `src/main.js` (game loop, init order).
    43	- **Entities** (things with position/state) go in `src/entities/`.
    44	- **Systems** (behaviors, effects, UI) go in `src/systems/`.

Also notable: this dispatch's stream kept going AFTER the commit landed at `c3e3819` (the visible terminal tail showed `finish_reason=stop ctok=301` but later chat-monitor events showed the same session sending 3-4 more 4096-token (truncated) responses + a few smaller ones. Lesson: dispatches that hit truncation can spin without value — worth investigating whether `--max-tokens 4096` is high enough to fit hip's final wrap-up response, or if the auto-continue-on-length logic in agent.rs is firing more than once for the same trailing thought.

Post-mortem:

First version of the edit used `floorCount` which was declared LATER in the file (the variant block is inserted BEFORE the windows block where floorCount is defined). Hip noticed the lexical ordering issue immediately and fixed it by inlining `Math.max(1, Math.floor(h / 3))`. Single self-correcting edit. This is a real test of the model's static-analysis instinct — it didn't wait for the runtime error.

     4	Top-level entry point; wires all entities, systems, and scene modules; sets up game loop, renderer, and input handling.
     5	
     6	## src/entities/
     7	- `player.js` — Player character: movement, health, state, input handling.
     8	- `enemy.js` — Enemy AI: spawning, chasing, attacking, death.
     9	- `npcs.js` — Civilian NPCs: wandering, fleeing, idle behavior.
    10	- `vehicle.js` — Drivable vehicles: physics, collision, player entry/exit.
    11	- `police.js` — Police units: pursuit, wanted-level response.
    12	- `pickups.js` — Collectible items: health packs, ammo, score pickups.
    13	- `barrels.js` — Destructible barrels: explosion triggers, placement.
    14	- `target.js` — Target dummies: shooting practice, hit detection.
    15	
    16	## src/systems/
    17	- `shooting.js` — Raycast/projectile shooting mechanics.
    18	- `weapons.js` — Weapon definitions, switching, stats, ammo.
    19	- `audio.js` — SFX playback (shots, explosions, pickups).
    20	- `music.js` — Background music, dynamic intensity layers.
    21	- `missions.js` — Mission objectives, completion tracking.
    22	- `minimap.js` — Radar/minimap rendering and entity markers.
    23	- `wanted.js` — Wanted level system, police escalation.
    24	- `grenades.js` — Grenade throwing, arming, explosion logic.
    25	- `particles.js` — Particle effects (explosions, smoke, sparks).
    26	- `weather.js` — Weather effects (rain, fog, visibility).
    27	- `save.js` — Save/load game state to localStorage.
    28	- `pause.js` — Pause menu, game state freeze.
    29	- `hit-marker.js` — Hit feedback visual markers.
    30	- `stamina.js` — Stamina bar for sprinting/exertion.
    31	- `streak.js` — Kill streak tracking and rewards.
    32	- `muzzle-flash.js` — Muzzle flash visual effects.
    33	- `feedback.js` — Screen shake, damage flash, general feedback.
    34	
    35	## src/scene/
    36	- `city.js` — City buildings, streets, urban geometry.
    37	- `world.js` — World container, terrain, skybox setup.
    38	- `props.js` — Static props (crates, signs, furniture).
    39	- `mountains.js` — Distant mountain geometry, backdrop.
    40	
    41	## How to add a new feature
    42	- **Top-level wiring:** import and register in `src/main.js` (game loop, init order).
    43	- **Entities** (things with position/state) go in `src/entities/`.
    44	- **Systems** (behaviors, effects, UI) go in `src/systems/`.

src/scene/city.js
Post-mortem:

Hip identified the existing per-edge sidewalk loop and **extended it** with the prop spawn rather than adding a parallel loop. That's the right pattern — colocates prop position logic with sidewalk position logic (uses the same edge coordinates). Net +43 lines, build clean. If perf becomes an issue with ~1100 props city-wide, the natural fix is to lower the per-edge count from 2 to 1 or skip via Math.random() < 0.5.

src/scene/city.js
Post-mortem:

Hip executed step 1 (search), step 2 (edit, +17 lines), step 3 (`git add`) but stopped without running step 4 (commit) or step 5 (build). The final assistant turn was `out=11` — meaning hip's wrap-up response was tiny, suggesting it thought it was "done" after the edit landed. Orchestrator committed via direct git + ran build. Build clean, console clean. The iter 23/25 lesson note in LOOP_RULES says "commit BEFORE build verify, with explicit YOU MUST RUN THE git commit STEP line." We HAVE that line in the prompt now. It still didn't help here. New hypothesis: the model treats `git add` as a sufficient terminal action when the file change is small. Possible mitigation: combine add+commit into a single shell command (`git add ... && git commit -m '...'`) so the model sees ONE shell action that does both, rather than two separate steps it can stop between.

src/scene/world.js
Post-mortem:

World.js already had a `createGradientSky` shader-based helper from earlier work. Hip just swapped the color params from sunset (0x6da8d8 + 0xffc4a0) to cinematic blue (0x4a8ad8 + 0xc7e8ff) and matched the fog. 2-line surgical change. One hiccup: hip's very first git command came back "Nothing specified, nothing added" (wrong path on first try) — it then re-anchored, re-read AGENTS.md to confirm world.js path, did the edit + combined add+commit successfully. Net cost: 1 retry. Combined add+commit pattern continues to hold.

[0;33mpath[0m:  /Users/dan/.hip-loop/3d-shooter/src/scene/world.js
[ok]      1	// Static world: ground, sky color, simple lighting. Future iterations
     2	// add buildings/props here or factor into separate sub-modules.
     3	import * as THREE from 'three';
     4	
     5	const CYCLE = 90; // seconds for full day/night loop
     6	const PHASE_LEN = 22.5; // each phase duration
     7	
     8	const PHASES = [
     9	  { name: 'dawn',  sunPos: [-60, 15, 20], sunColor: 0x88aacc, sunIntensity: 1.0, sky: 0x88aacc, fog: 0x88aacc, fogDensity: 0.006, streetlight: 0.5, ambient: 0x6688aa, ambientIntensity: 0.35 },
    10	  { name: 'day',   sunPos: [40, 60, 20],  sunColor: 0xffffff, sunIntensity: 1.4, sky: 0x6da8d8, fog: 0x6da8d8, fogDensity: 0.004, streetlight: 0   , ambient: 0xb0c4de, ambientIntensity: 0.45 },
    11	  { name: 'dusk',  sunPos: [60, 15, 20],   sunColor: 0xff9966, sunIntensity: 1.0, sky: 0xd68b5a, fog: 0xd68b5a, fogDensity: 0.008, streetlight: 0.5, ambient: 0x885533, ambientIntensity: 0.3 },
    12	  { name: 'night', sunPos: [0, -5, 20],    sunColor: 0x334466, sunIntensity: 0.05, sky: 0x0a1426, fog: 0x0a1426, fogDensity: 0.015, streetlight: 1.5, ambient: 0x1a2244, ambientIntensity: 0.15 },
    13	];
    14	
    15	function lerp(a, b, t) { return a + (b - a) * t; }
    16	function lerpColor(c1, c2, t) {
    17	  const a = new THREE.Color(c1);
    18	  const b = new THREE.Color(c2);
    19	  return a.lerp(b, t).getHex();
    20	}
    21	
    22	// Procedural skybox: vertical gradient (topColor -> bottomColor) via a large sphere with custom shader
    23	let _skyMesh = null;
    24	
    25	function createGradientSky(scene, topColor, bottomColor) {
    26	  if (_skyMesh) scene.remove(_skyMesh);
    27	
    28	  const skyGeo = new THREE.SphereGeometry(250, 32, 15);
    29	  const skyMat = new THREE.ShaderMaterial({
    30	    side: THREE.BackSide,
    31	    depthWrite: false,
    32	    uniforms: {
    33	      topColor: { value: new THREE.Color(topColor) },
    34	      bottomColor: { value: new THREE.Color(bottomColor) },
    35	    },
    36	    vertexShader: `
    37	      varying vec3 vWorldPos;
    38	      void main() {
    39	        vec4 wp = modelMatrix * vec4(position, 1.0);
    40	        vWorldPos = wp.xyz;
    41	        gl_Position = projectionMatrix * viewMatrix * wp;
    42	      }
    43	    `,
    44	    fragmentShader: `
    45	      uniform vec3 topColor;
    46	      uniform vec3 bottomColor;
    47	      varying vec3 vWorldPos;
    48	      void main() {
    49	        float h = clamp(normalize(vWorldPos).y, -1.0, 1.0);
    50	        float t = (h + 1.0) * 0.5; // 0 at bottom, 1 at top
    51	        gl_FragColor = vec4(mix(bottomColor, topColor, t), 1.0);
    52	      }
    53	    `,
    54	  });
    55	  _skyMesh = new THREE.Mesh(skyGeo, skyMat);
    56	  scene.add(_skyMesh);
    57	  return _skyMesh;
    58	}
    59	
    60	function updateGradientSky(topColor, bottomColor) {
    61	  if (_skyMesh) {
    62	    _skyMesh.material.uniforms.topColor.value.set(topColor);
    63	    _skyMesh.material.uniforms.bottomColor.value.set(bottomColor);
    64	  }
    65	}
    66	
    67	export function createWorld(scene, city) {
    68	  // Sunset gradient: light blue top -> soft pink horizon
    69	  createGradientSky(scene, 0x6da8d8, 0xffc4a0);
    70	  scene.background = null; // shader sky replaces solid color
    71	  scene.fog = new THREE.FogExp2(0x2244aa, 0.008);
    72	
    73	  const sun = new THREE.DirectionalLight(0xffffff, 1.4);
    74	  sun.position.set(40, 60, 20);
    75	  sun.castShadow = true;
    76	  sun.shadow.mapSize.set(2048, 2048);
    77	  sun.shadow.camera.left = -120;
    78	  sun.shadow.camera.right = 120;
    79	  sun.shadow.camera.top = 120;
    80	  sun.shadow.camera.bottom = -120;
    81	  scene.add(sun);
    82	  scene.add(new THREE.AmbientLight(0xb0c4de, 0.45));
    83	
    84	  // Ground: green base with faint grid overlay
    85	  const gridCanvas = document.createElement('canvas');
    86	  gridCanvas.width = 512;
    87	  gridCanvas.height = 512;
    88	  const gctx = gridCanvas.getContext('2d');
    89	  gctx.fillStyle = '#4a6f3a';
    90	  gctx.fillRect(0, 0, 512, 512);
    91	  gctx.strokeStyle = 'rgba(0,0,0,0.12)';
    92	  gctx.lineWidth = 1;
    93	  const step = 51.2; // 512/10 → 10u intervals when texture covers 512u
    94	  for (let i = 0; i <= 512; i += step) {
    95	    gctx.beginPath(); gctx.moveTo(i, 0); gctx.lineTo(i, 512); gctx.stroke();
    96	    gctx.beginPath(); gctx.moveTo(0, i); gctx.lineTo(512, i); gctx.stroke();
    97	  }
    98	  const gridTexture = new THREE.CanvasTexture(gridCanvas);
    99	  gridTexture.wrapS = gridTexture.wrapT = THREE.RepeatWrapping;
   100	  gridTexture.repeat.set(10, 10); // 512u / 10 = 51.2u per tile → 10u grid spacing
   101	  const ground = new THREE.Mesh(
   102	    new THREE.PlaneGeometry(500, 500),
   103	    new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ map: gridTexture, roughness: 0.95 })
   104	  );
   105	  ground.rotation.x = -Math.PI / 2;
   106	  ground.receiveShadow = true;
   107	  scene.add(ground);
   108	
   109	  let _currentPhase = 'day';
   110	  let _timeOfDay = 0;
   111	
   112	  // Set initial state
   113	  if (city) city.setStreetlightIntensity(0);
   114	
   115	  return {
   116	    currentPhase() { return _currentPhase; },
   117	    getTimeOfDay() { return _timeOfDay; },
   118	
   119	    update(dt, t) {
   120	      const cycleT = (t % CYCLE) / CYCLE; // 0..1
   121	      _timeOfDay = cycleT;
   122	
   123	      const phaseIdx = Math.floor(cycleT * 4) % 4;
   124	      const nextIdx  = (phaseIdx + 1) % 4;
   125	      const localT   = (cycleT * 4) % 1; // 0..1 within phase
   126	      const smoothT  = localT * localT * (3 - 2 * localT); // smoothstep
   127	
   128	      const from = PHASES[phaseIdx];
   129	      const to   = PHASES[nextIdx];
   130	
   131	      // Interpolate sun position
   132	      const sx = lerp(from.sunPos[0], to.sunPos[0], smoothT);
   133	      const sy = lerp(from.sunPos[1], to.sunPos[1], smoothT);
   134	      const sz = lerp(from.sunPos[2], to.sunPos[2], smoothT);
   135	      sun.position.set(sx, sy, sz);
   136	
   137	      // Interpolate sun color & intensity
   138	      sun.color.setHex(lerpColor(from.sunColor, to.sunColor, smoothT));
   139	      sun.intensity = lerp(from.sunIntensity, to.sunIntensity, smoothT);
   140	
   141	      // Interpolate sky gradient / fog
   142	      const skyColor = lerpColor(from.sky, to.sky, smoothT);
   143	      const horizonColor = lerpColor(from.fog, to.fog, smoothT);
   144	      updateGradientSky(skyColor, horizonColor);
   145	      scene.fog.color.setHex(horizonColor);
   146	
   147	      // Streetlights
   148	      if (city) {
   149	        const sl = lerp(from.streetlight, to.streetlight, smoothT);
   150	        city.setStreetlightIntensity(sl);
   151	      }
   152	
   153	      _currentPhase = from.name;
   154	    },
   155	  };
   156	}

c317a16 iter 82: yellow road center-line stripes +27 -0
src/scene/city.js
Post-mortem:

Same shape as iter 75: commit landed cleanly at `c317a16` after ~2 min of actual work, then `finish_reason=length` triggered the agent's `auto_continue_on_length` 4-5 times in a row. Each iteration produced 4096 ctok of "continuation" output that wasn't useful (no new commits, no edits). Total wasted: ~20K ctok / ~6 min of wall time. **Hypothesis for the recurring overrun**: the model's wrap-up response after the commit + build is generating a long-form rationale that hits 4096 tokens, triggers the truncation, and the auto-continue logic in `agent.rs` interprets that as "needs to keep going" rather than "model meandered into a stuck loop." The fix is probably in two places: (a) bump `--max-tokens` from 4096 to 8192 for these dispatches so the wrap-up fits in one shot, OR (b) tighten the auto-continue heuristic to stop after 1 truncation if the previous round had no tool calls (i.e. the model is just talking to itself). Both iters 75 and 82 happened during single-file dispatches with substantial structural edits (~25-30+ lines). The model seems to over-narrate after these. Worth investigating.

     2	
     3	## src/main.js
     4	Top-level entry point; wires all entities, systems, and scene modules; sets up game loop, renderer, and input handling.
     5	
     6	## src/entities/
     7	- `player.js` — Player character: movement, health, state, input handling.
     8	- `enemy.js` — Enemy AI: spawning, chasing, attacking, death.
     9	- `npcs.js` — Civilian NPCs: wandering, fleeing, idle behavior.
    10	- `vehicle.js` — Drivable vehicles: physics, collision, player entry/exit.
    11	- `police.js` — Police units: pursuit, wanted-level response.
    12	- `pickups.js` — Collectible items: health packs, ammo, score pickups.
    13	- `barrels.js` — Destructible barrels: explosion triggers, placement.
    14	- `target.js` — Target dummies: shooting practice, hit detection.
    15	
    16	## src/systems/
    17	- `shooting.js` — Raycast/projectile shooting mechanics.
    18	- `weapons.js` — Weapon definitions, switching, stats, ammo.
    19	- `audio.js` — SFX playback (shots, explosions, pickups).
    20	- `music.js` — Background music, dynamic intensity layers.
    21	- `missions.js` — Mission objectives, completion tracking.
    22	- `minimap.js` — Radar/minimap rendering and entity markers.
    23	- `wanted.js` — Wanted level system, police escalation.
    24	- `grenades.js` — Grenade throwing, arming, explosion logic.
    25	- `particles.js` — Particle effects (explosions, smoke, sparks).
    26	- `weather.js` — Weather effects (rain, fog, visibility).
    27	- `save.js` — Save/load game state to localStorage.
    28	- `pause.js` — Pause menu, game state freeze.
    29	- `hit-marker.js` — Hit feedback visual markers.
    30	- `stamina.js` — Stamina bar for sprinting/exertion.
    31	- `streak.js` — Kill streak tracking and rewards.
    32	- `muzzle-flash.js` — Muzzle flash visual effects.
    33	- `feedback.js` — Screen shake, damage flash, general feedback.
    34	
    35	## src/scene/
    36	- `city.js` — City buildings, streets, urban geometry.
    37	- `world.js` — World container, terrain, skybox setup.
    38	- `props.js` — Static props (crates, signs, furniture).
    39	- `mountains.js` — Distant mountain geometry, backdrop.
    40	
    41	## How to add a new feature
    42	- **Top-level wiring:** import and register in `src/main.js` (game loop, init order).
    43	- **Entities** (things with position/state) go in `src/entities/`.
    44	- **Systems** (behaviors, effects, UI) go in `src/systems/`.

[ok]      1	export function createClouds(THREE, opts = {}) {
     2	  const count = opts.count ?? 14;
     3	  const range = opts.range ?? 200;
     4	  const minY = opts.minY ?? 35;
     5	  const maxY = opts.maxY ?? 45;
     6	  const driftSpeed = opts.driftSpeed ?? 2.5;
     7	  const group = new THREE.Group();
     8	  const clouds = [];
     9	
    10	  for (let i = 0; i < count; i++) {
    11	    const cloud = new THREE.Group();
    12	    const puffs = Math.floor(3 + Math.random() * 3);
    13	    for (let p = 0; p < puffs; p++) {
    14	      const w = 4 + Math.random() * 5;
    15	      const h = 1 + Math.random();
    16	      const d = 4 + Math.random() * 5;
    17	      const puff = new THREE.Mesh(
    18	        new THREE.BoxGeometry(w, h, d),
    19	        new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ color: 0xffffff, roughness: 0.95 }),
    20	      );
    21	      puff.position.set(
    22	        (Math.random() - 0.5) * 6,
    23	        (Math.random() - 0.5) * 1,
    24	        (Math.random() - 0.5) * 6,
    25	      );
    26	      cloud.add(puff);
    27	    }
    28	    cloud.position.set(
    29	      (Math.random() - 0.5) * range * 2,
    30	      minY + Math.random() * (maxY - minY),
    31	      (Math.random() - 0.5) * range * 2,
    32	    );
    33	    group.add(cloud);
    34	    clouds.push(cloud);
    35	  }
    36	
    37	  function update(dt) {
    38	    const drift = dt * driftSpeed;

              function update(dt, playerPos) {
                const t = performance.now() / 1000;
                for (const d of dogs) {

                  const dz = d.mesh.position.z - playerPos.z;

                  const dist = d.mesh.position.distanceTo(d.target);
                  if (dist < 1 || d.timer > 8) {

                  const dir = new THREE.Vector3().subVectors(d.target, d.mesh.position);

                  const speed = 2;

                    dir.normalize();
                    d.mesh.position.x += dir.x * speed * dt;
                    d.mesh.position.z += dir.z * speed * dt;
                    d.mesh.rotation.y = Math.atan2(dir.x, dir.z);

                  }
                  d.head.rotation.x = Math.sin(t * 3 + d.phase) * 0.1;
                }
            
                for (const b of birds) {
                  b.angle += b.speed * dt;
                  b.mesh.position.x = b.centerX + Math.cos(b.angle) * b.radius;
                  b.mesh.position.z = b.centerZ + Math.sin(b.angle) * b.radius;
                  b.mesh.position.y = b.altitude;
                  b.mesh.rotation.y = -b.angle + Math.PI / 2;
                  const flap = Math.sin(t * 8) * 0.3;

                  b.rightWing.rotation.z = -flap;
                }
              }

[ok]      1	# AGENTS.md — Project Module Map
     2	
     3	## src/main.js
     4	Top-level entry point; wires all entities, systems, and scene modules; sets up game loop, renderer, and input handling.
     5	
     6	## src/entities/
     7	- `player.js` — Player character: movement, health, state, input handling.
     8	- `enemy.js` — Enemy AI: spawning, chasing, attacking, death.
     9	- `npcs.js` — Civilian NPCs: wandering, fleeing, idle behavior.
    10	- `vehicle.js` — Drivable vehicles: physics, collision, player entry/exit.
    11	- `police.js` — Police units: pursuit, wanted-level response.
    12	- `pickups.js` — Collectible items: health packs, ammo, score pickups.
    13	- `barrels.js` — Destructible barrels: explosion triggers, placement.
    14	- `target.js` — Target dummies: shooting practice, hit detection.
    15	
    16	## src/systems/
    17	- `shooting.js` — Raycast/projectile shooting mechanics.
    18	- `weapons.js` — Weapon definitions, switching, stats, ammo.
    19	- `audio.js` — SFX playback (shots, explosions, pickups).
    20	- `music.js` — Background music, dynamic intensity layers.
    21	- `missions.js` — Mission objectives, completion tracking.
    22	- `minimap.js` — Radar/minimap rendering and entity markers.
    23	- `wanted.js` — Wanted level system, police escalation.
    24	- `grenades.js` — Grenade throwing, arming, explosion logic.
    25	- `particles.js` — Particle effects (explosions, smoke, sparks).
    26	- `weather.js` — Weather effects (rain, fog, visibility).
    27	- `save.js` — Save/load game state to localStorage.
    28	- `pause.js` — Pause menu, game state freeze.
    29	- `hit-marker.js` — Hit feedback visual markers.
    30	- `stamina.js` — Stamina bar for sprinting/exertion.
    31	- `streak.js` — Kill streak tracking and rewards.
    32	- `muzzle-flash.js` — Muzzle flash visual effects.
    33	- `feedback.js` — Screen shake, damage flash, general feedback.
    34	
    35	## src/scene/
    36	- `city.js` — City buildings, streets, urban geometry.
    37	- `world.js` — World container, terrain, skybox setup.
    38	- `props.js` — Static props (crates, signs, furniture).
    39	- `mountains.js` — Distant mountain geometry, backdrop.
    40	
    41	## How to add a new feature
    42	- **Top-level wiring:** import and register in `src/main.js` (game loop, init order).
    43	- **Entities** (things with position/state) go in `src/entities/`.
    44	- **Systems** (behaviors, effects, UI) go in `src/systems/`.

Post-mortem:

Iter 88's hip ran 3 rounds total: tool calls (edit) → final response with `ctok=1` — meaning the model jumped straight to a final response after the edit landed, skipping the bash steps entirely. Even with the combined `&&` shell command in the prompt. The orchestrator caught it via `git status` and committed manually. Total cost: 1 extra orchestrator command. **This is a regression of the combined-shell rule for short-burst dispatches** — when the model decides to wrap up after 3 rounds it skips ALL subsequent steps including bash. Possible mitigation: rephrase step 3 as a tool action ("call bash with command:") instead of a numbered procedure item.

[0;33mpath[0m:  /Users/dan/.hip-loop/3d-shooter/AGENTS.md
[ok]      1	# AGENTS.md — Project Module Map
     2	
     3	## src/main.js
     4	Top-level entry point; wires all entities, systems, and scene modules; sets up game loop, renderer, and input handling.
     5	
     6	## src/entities/
     7	- `player.js` — Player character: movement, health, state, input handling.
     8	- `enemy.js` — Enemy AI: spawning, chasing, attacking, death.
     9	- `npcs.js` — Civilian NPCs: wandering, fleeing, idle behavior.
    10	- `vehicle.js` — Drivable vehicles: physics, collision, player entry/exit.
    11	- `police.js` — Police units: pursuit, wanted-level response.
    12	- `pickups.js` — Collectible items: health packs, ammo, score pickups.
    13	- `barrels.js` — Destructible barrels: explosion triggers, placement.
    14	- `target.js` — Target dummies: shooting practice, hit detection.
    15	
    16	## src/systems/
    17	- `shooting.js` — Raycast/projectile shooting mechanics.
    18	- `weapons.js` — Weapon definitions, switching, stats, ammo.
    19	- `audio.js` — SFX playback (shots, explosions, pickups).
    20	- `music.js` — Background music, dynamic intensity layers.
    21	- `missions.js` — Mission objectives, completion tracking.
    22	- `minimap.js` — Radar/minimap rendering and entity markers.
    23	- `wanted.js` — Wanted level system, police escalation.
    24	- `grenades.js` — Grenade throwing, arming, explosion logic.
    25	- `particles.js` — Particle effects (explosions, smoke, sparks).
    26	- `weather.js` — Weather effects (rain, fog, visibility).
    27	- `save.js` — Save/load game state to localStorage.
    28	- `pause.js` — Pause menu, game state freeze.
    29	- `hit-marker.js` — Hit feedback visual markers.
    30	- `stamina.js` — Stamina bar for sprinting/exertion.
    31	- `streak.js` — Kill streak tracking and rewards.
    32	- `muzzle-flash.js` — Muzzle flash visual effects.
    33	- `feedback.js` — Screen shake, damage flash, general feedback.
    34	
    35	## src/scene/
    36	- `city.js` — City buildings, streets, urban geometry.
    37	- `world.js` — World container, terrain, skybox setup.
    38	- `props.js` — Static props (crates, signs, furniture).
    39	- `mountains.js` — Distant mountain geometry, backdrop.
    40	
    41	## How to add a new feature
    42	- **Top-level wiring:** import and register in `src/main.js` (game loop, init order).
    43	- **Entities** (things with position/state) go in `src/entities/`.
    44	- **Systems** (behaviors, effects, UI) go in `src/systems/`.

[0;33mnew_string[0m:  // Helper to create parked planes near hangar
              function makeParkedPlane(x, z, color, rotY) {
                const p = new THREE.Group();
                const fuselage = new THREE.Mesh(
                  new THREE.CylinderGeometry(0.6, 0.6, 8),
                  new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ color })
                );
                fuselage.rotation.z = Math.PI / 2;
                fuselage.position.set(0, 1, 0);
                p.add(fuselage);
                const wings = new THREE.Mesh(
                  new THREE.BoxGeometry(2.5, 0.1, 8),
                  new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ color: 0xcccccc })
                );
                wings.position.set(0, 1, 0);
                p.add(wings);
                const tail = new THREE.Mesh(
                  new THREE.BoxGeometry(1.5, 1.5, 0.2),
                  new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ color: 0xcccccc })
                );
                tail.position.set(-3.5, 1, 0);
                p.add(tail);
                const vStab = new THREE.Mesh(
                  new THREE.BoxGeometry(0.2, 1.4, 1.2),
                  new THREE.MeshStandardMaterial({ color: 0xcccccc })
                );
                vStab.position.set(-3.5, 1.7, 0);
                p.add(vStab);
                p.position.set(x, 0.2, z);
                p.rotation.y = rotY;
                return p;
              }
            
              group.add(makeParkedPlane(10, 14, 0xc83030, Math.PI / 4));
              group.add(makeParkedPlane(-10, 14, 0x4488ff, -Math.PI / 4));
            
              return { group };

[ok]      1	# AGENTS.md — Project Module Map
     2	
     3	## src/main.js
     4	Top-level entry point; wires all entities, systems, and scene modules; sets up game loop, renderer, and input handling.
     5	
     6	## src/entities/
     7	- `player.js` — Player character: movement, health, state, input handling.
     8	- `enemy.js` — Enemy AI: spawning, chasing, attacking, death.
     9	- `npcs.js` — Civilian NPCs: wandering, fleeing, idle behavior.
    10	- `vehicle.js` — Drivable vehicles: physics, collision, player entry/exit.
    11	- `police.js` — Police units: pursuit, wanted-level response.
    12	- `pickups.js` — Collectible items: health packs, ammo, score pickups.
    13	- `barrels.js` — Destructible barrels: explosion triggers, placement.
    14	- `target.js` — Target dummies: shooting practice, hit detection.
    15	
    16	## src/systems/
    17	- `shooting.js` — Raycast/projectile shooting mechanics.
    18	- `weapons.js` — Weapon definitions, switching, stats, ammo.
    19	- `audio.js` — SFX playback (shots, explosions, pickups).
    20	- `music.js` — Background music, dynamic intensity layers.
    21	- `missions.js` — Mission objectives, completion tracking.
    22	- `minimap.js` — Radar/minimap rendering and entity markers.
    23	- `wanted.js` — Wanted level system, police escalation.
    24	- `grenades.js` — Grenade throwing, arming, explosion logic.
    25	- `particles.js` — Particle effects (explosions, smoke, sparks).
    26	- `weather.js` — Weather effects (rain, fog, visibility).
    27	- `save.js` — Save/load game state to localStorage.
    28	- `pause.js` — Pause menu, game state freeze.
    29	- `hit-marker.js` — Hit feedback visual markers.
    30	- `stamina.js` — Stamina bar for sprinting/exertion.
    31	- `streak.js` — Kill streak tracking and rewards.
    32	- `muzzle-flash.js` — Muzzle flash visual effects.
    33	- `feedback.js` — Screen shake, damage flash, general feedback.
    34	
    35	## src/scene/
    36	- `city.js` — City buildings, streets, urban geometry.
    37	- `world.js` — World container, terrain, skybox setup.
    38	- `props.js` — Static props (crates, signs, furniture).
    39	- `mountains.js` — Distant mountain geometry, backdrop.
    40	
    41	## How to add a new feature
    42	- **Top-level wiring:** import and register in `src/main.js` (game loop, init order).
    43	- **Entities** (things with position/state) go in `src/entities/`.
    44	- **Systems** (behaviors, effects, UI) go in `src/systems/`.

Post-mortem:

First attempt added a pier with `const pillarGeo = ...` — collision with the existing dock pillar variable in the same function scope (lake.js had pillarGeo from iter 63). Build failed with `Identifier "pillarGeo" has already been declared`. Hip caught the error from the build output, made a 2-line fix renaming to `pierPillarGeo`, committed the fix separately, re-ran build, passed. **Notable: hip did NOT need orchestrator intervention.** It read the error message, identified the cause, surgical-fixed it, and re-verified. Best demonstrated self-recovery in the whole run.
